<USER_REQUEST>
The 1st module should be named as AST.py as it is regarding the Abstract Syntax Tree used for storing the terms, 1st order formulae and propositional formulae. You have to think about which data structure to use for this. I think that linked list will be good because then we can easily merge 2 or more long terms to create a larger term and so on. But we may need to change the structure later if we need. The nodes will be the various types of symbols used in 1st order logic and propositional logic.
All the nodes must be uniquely identified by their names which is a string. 

For terms, we need to have a variable type node and a function type node. A function will also have an arity which will be of unsigned int type. Additionally, there will also be a dummy variable node which will act as a placeholder for terms, which will be used later for term replacement purposes you will know later. Though 1st order logic also talks about constants but ZFC does not need it so we can avoid that.

For 1st order formulae, we will have above kind of nodes, alongwith a relation node which will also have an arity of unsigned int type. Also there will logical connectives which are ¬, ∧, ∨, ⇒, ⇔. Also there will be quantifiers which are ∀, ∃, ∃!. Additionally, we will also have a meta-variable node which act as placeholder for 1st order formulae. Its use will be evident much later when we code for advanced proving techniques much later, so you can leave it empty for now.

For propositional formula, we will have propositional variables and the 5 logical connectives which I mentioned above.

You can also have brackets and whitespaces as special nodes as they are not part of the 1st order logic but they help in making the terms and formulae look clean.

Just create a file for holding these data structures. Further information will be evident from next module.
</USER_REQUEST>

<USER_REQUEST>
/grill-me Wonderful. Now we move to one of the toughest tasks of this project which is to create a parser and lexer. You have to create a file Frontend.py which basically takes a string as input from the user and correspondingly create the term, 1st order formula or propositional formula.

Basically there will be 3 functions, one for creating terms, one for for 1st order formula and 1 for propositional formula. While typing the string, the user can only use already defined variables, functions, relations etc. For example, the user can't type "x = 3" if the user has not already defined x as a variable. In such cases, it should report an unrecognised symbol error to the user.

The user may enter brackets and whitespaces anywhere in the term or formulae which he types, as long as the brackets are balanced. If the brackets are not balanced, then report that error to the user.

The tricky thing is that which you have to keep in mind is that just like normal people, the user will always use infix notation for binary logical connectives, binary functions and binary relations whereas postfix notation for higher arity functions and relations. Also unary operators will have higher precedence as compared binary operators for example "- 3 + 5" will mean "2" and not "-8". Similarly "¬ p ∨ q" is equivalent to "(¬p) ∨ q" and not "¬(p ∨ q)".

Quantifiers will always have highest precedence i.e. the non-whitespace symbol occuring just after a quantifier must be a variable, otherwise an error must be shown to the user. Just after this variable, the scope of the quantifier will be written. If the next non-whitespace character just after the variable is an opening bracket, then its correspondingly closing bracket will marke the end of the scope of the quantifier. If it is not an opening bracket, then it will be understood that the scope ends at the end of the line.

Obviously propositional formulae and 1st order formulae should not be mixed, for example "P ∧ x = 3" makes no sense.

Since brackets and spaces are not actually part of the 1st order logic or propositional logic, it will be tempting to drop them and simplify the string in postfix notation then create AST which would have been simpler. But the challenge is that I want that the exact user's input string should be recoverable from the AST(i.e. with exact same placing of brackets and white spaces). This is necessary because I want the user to be able to see what term/formula has he created and how they are exactly being modified.

If you have any queries regarding this, then you can ask me. Otherwise create the file then test this on streamlit by asking the user to enter a term, a 1st order formula and a propositional formula in a textbox and then saving it in the environment.
</USER_REQUEST>

<USER_REQUEST>
Fine, our next module to design will be SubstitutionManager.py. Its basic tasks will be to be able to perform replacements in terms and formulae.

First of all, you have to create a function "get_free" which inputs a 1st order formula and returns the set of all free variables in it. Another function "get_bound" would return bounded variables. Similarly "check_free" function will input a 1st order function and a variable then return true iff that variable is free in that function. Similarly create "check_bound" function. Now you will automatically understand in which future functions, you will be needing to call these 4 important helper functions.

As an important side remark, I want to tell you that our program allows nested scoping of same variable, i.e. "∀x( x=3 ⇒ ∀x(x=5))" is a valid 1st order formula. Also it is possible that a variable is both free and bounded in a 1st order formula, eg:- "x=3 ∨ ∀x(x ∈ A)" is a valid formula. You have to be careful about certain edge cases because of this while designing the functions now and in future.

The next important helper function will be is_substitutable_free() which will take a variable, a term and a 1st order formula, then return true iff replacing all free occurences of the variable in the 1st order formula with the term does not change the semantic meaning of the formula. Similarly write is_substitutable_bounded() which checks whether substituting all bouned occurences of a variable with another one will change the meaning or not. Also create a variant of these 2 functions which will also accept an unsigned integer(say n) where only the n_th occurence of the variable(free or bounded) will be changed.

Then you have to write substitute_free() function which substitutes a variable for a term in a 1st order formula irrespective of meaning is changed or not. Similarly also write a substitute_bound() function. Also create substitute_all() function combining the functions of above 2. Similarly create substitute_term() function to replace all
<truncated 316 bytes>
te a find_substituted() function which takes 2 1st order formulae as input and then checks if it possible to create the 2nd formula from 1st one by replacing all occurences of a single variable with a term. If so, then return that term. If not possible then return None. If both the formula are exactly same, then return any true. This helper function will be used later in an inference rule.

In order to use these program, we will add some new commands in the main REPL loop:-
1. "st t1 x t2 t3" -> replace all occurences of variable named x in term named t1 with term named t2 and save the new term with name t3 in environment.
2. "st t1 x t2 t3 3" -> the same as above but only at the 3rd index(starting index is 1).
3. "sf f1 x t1 f2" -> replace all free occurence of variable x in 1st order formula f1 with term t1 and save the newly created formula with name f2 in environment. In case it is not substitutable, then mention this in the terminal else not. In case f1 was an already proven theorem(check from environment) and x is substitutable with t1, the f2 will ALSO be saved as a new proven theorem with the same name and definition in the environment.
4. "sf f1 x t1 f2 2" -> Same as above but at 2nd index.
5. "sb f1 x t1 f2" and "sb f1 x t1 f2 2" -> Same as above 2 with bounded variables.
6. "sa f1 x t1 f2" and "sa f1 x t1 f2 2"-> Same as above but with all variables.
7. "sp P1 q P2 P3" -> replace all occurences of propositional variable named p in propositional formula named P1 with propositional formula named P2. Save the newly formed propositional formula with name P3 in environment.

<USER_REQUEST>
Our next module will be DeductiveSystem.py which will store the logical axioms and inference rules of the 1st order logic. The logical axioms will be functions which will take a 1st order formula as input and return true iff it satisfies the conditions of that axioms. The inference rules will also be functions which will take a set of proven theorems called premises and a conclusion formula to prove. It will also return true iff the conditions of the inference rule are satisfied. We will have 5 logical axioms:-

1. E1(reflexivity of equality)
2. E2(variable replacement in function) -> (x1 = y1 ∧ ... xn = yn) ⇒ (f(x1, ... xn) = f(y1, ... yn))
3. E3(variable replacement in relation) -> (x1 = y1 ∧ ... xn = yn) ⇒ (R(x1, ... xn) ⇒ R(y1, ... yn))
4. Q1(Universal instantiation) ∀x φ ⇒ (x substituted for t in φ) if substitutable
5. Q2(Existential generalisation) (x substituted for t in φ) ⇒ ∃x φ if substitutable

We will have 4 inference rules:-

1. QR1:- {ψ ⇒ φ} ψ ⇒ (∀xφ) where x is not free in ψ and not bounded in φ
2. QR2:- {φ ⇒ ψ} (∃xφ) ⇒ ψ where x is not free in ψ and not bounded in φ
3. PC1:- Create a propositional formula from the 1st order formula by replacing atomic formulae and quantifier formulae by propositional variables. Then check validity of propositional variables by truth table.
4. PC2:- Same as above but use sequent calculus instead

After this we will add a new REPL commands to prove theorems:-

1. "ua E1 f1" -> It will use the axiom E1 to prove the formula named f1. If succesful, then f1 will ALSO be stored as a proven theorem with the same name in environment. In place of E1, it can be E2, E3, Q1, Q2, extension, regularity, union, pair, power, infinity, choice, specification, replacement.
2. "ir PC1 f1 f2 f3 ... fn" -> It will 1st check whether f2, f3 ... fn are already proven theorem names in environment or not. If so then it will use PC1 inference rule to prove 1st order formula f1. If succesful, then f1 will ALSO be stored as a proven theorem. In place of PC1, we can also use QR1, QR2, PC2.
3. "dt f1" -> Deletes an already proven theorem f1 from the environment. Note that this operation will always be safe, because even if it is deleted from the proven theorems, it will still be present as a created formula in the environment. All methods of proving ensure this.

</USER_REQUEST>

Fine. Now our next module will be DefinitionExpander.py. This will be comprising of functions for expanding terms and formulae IN-PLACE. Expanding a user-defined function or relation in a term or 1st order formula is simple using the information stored in the environment, so you can easily create a function for that.

Now suppose there is a 1st order formula Φ(F1(x1, x2 ... xm), y1, y2 ... yn) where F1 is an iota function derived from ∃! x Ψ(x, x1, x2 ... xm). Upon expansion, this should become ∃u (∀v (Ψ(u, x1, x2 ... xm) ⇔ u=v) ∧ Φ(u, y1, y2 ... yn)). Just check once if I have written the correct formula or not. Notice that this expansion requires 2 new variables u and v, so the iota expander function must also take these 2 variables as argument apart from the 1st order formula, the iota function's name and its position in the 1st order formula.

Additionally you also have to write a function which expands ∃x Ψ(x, v1, ...) into ¬∀x ¬Ψ(x, v1, ...). Similarly design another function which expands ∃!x Ψ(x, v1, ...) into ∃x ∀y(Ψ(y, v1, ...) ⇔ y=x), so it should take y also as input.

Finally, you have to add following REPL commands regarding expansion:-
1. "fold F1 3 t1 t2" -> Expand the user-defined function named F1 at the 3rd index in the term named t1. Save the newly created term as t2.
2. "fold F1 3 f1 f2" -> Same as above except that f1 and f2 are 1st order formulae. Additionally if f1 is already proven theorem then f2 will also become a proven theorem.
3. "fold R1 3 f1 f2" -> Same as above except R1 is user defined relation
4. "fold F1 3 f1 u v f2" -> Expand the iota function named F1 at index 3 in the 1st order formula named f1 by introducing the new variables named u and v. The program has to ensure that introduction of u and v does not change the semantic meaning of the formula, else report error to the user. If succesful, save the new formula with the name f2. Further if f1 was already proven then so will be f2.
5. "fold ∃ 3 f1 f2" -> Expand ∃ at 3rd index in 1st order formula f1 to get new formula f2. If f1 is proven, then so will be f2.
6. "fold ∃! 3 f1 y f2" -> Expand ∃!

If you have any doubts then ask me, else proceed
</USER_REQUEST>

<USER_REQUEST>
When a mathematician wants to prove a goal statement, he breaks it into sub-goals or lemmas which he try to prove. Once he proves a sub-goal, he almost forgets how he proved that, his entire focus comes back to proving the main goal. In order to implement this I want you to add a new REPL command "mission f1" where f1 is the name of a created formula which is not yet proven. This command will create a "child environment" which will have its own environment objects. It will be able to read the parent environment's objects but its own will be initially empty. The user will then try to prove the goal statement f1. Once it is proven then it should be displayed that the goal statement is proven so the child environment will be destroyed and all the child environment objects will be deleted. The parent environment will be just like before the child environment started, except that f1 is also a proven statement in parent environment.

Suppose somehow the user wants to terminate the child environment without proving the goal statement, then he can simply type exit. This will not prove the goal statement in parent environment, delete all child environment objects then delete the child environment. There is also a possibility that while being inside the child environment, the user types "mission f2" where f2 is the name of another formula created in either child or parent environment but not yet proven. This will create a "grandchild environment" with no objects initially. This process can continue any longer. Exiting will only delete the most recent environment. Every environment should be able to read the objects of all its ancestor environments. The "show" REPL command should display the objects of all the environments, one by one, starting from the "ground environment", which is the 1st environment created as soon as the program starts running. The ground environment is the only environment with no goal statement.
</USER_REQUEST>

The name of the file will be asked to the user. If that name already exists then report error. The format of the file should be in such a way that person can easily understand the file contents by looking at it and also easily modify them.
2. "load" which will ask the user the name of the save file to load. If the user enters the correct name then all the object of all the environments in that save file will be loaded and program will resume from that state.
3. "save_h" which will save the history of all the REPL commands typed by the user so far in the terminal since the program began executing or since the last history file was loaded. This history will be saved in a new file whose name will be asked by the user then saved in the history_files folder. The format of the file should be in such a way that person can easily understand the file contents by looking at it and also easily modify them.
4. "load_h" which will load the history file whose name is entered by the user. Loading the history file simply means running all the REPL commands in it in the correct sequence in the terminal. The way history files are saved, it ensures that the "exit" and "load_h" command will never come in the history file. However "save" and "save_h" commands can cause problems if present in history file, so they will simply be skipped while saving history files. Also for ske of convenience, also skip  "help" and "guide" commands from being saved in the history file. I hope no other REPL command can cause any problem when loaded.

If you feel that you need to create a lot of classes or functions for this, then you can do that in a new module StorageManager.py, else you can simply add them in any of the pre-existing modules

<USER_REQUEST>
I want you to create a new REPL command "auto f1" which attempts to prove the 1st order formula named f1 using all axioms and inference rules. If f1 is already proven theorem, then it mentions that in the terminal. Otherwise 1st, it will try to use all the axioms(both logical and non-logical) directly to prove it. If all of the axioms fail then it will move to QR1 and QR2 inference rules. These inference rules take exactly 1 premise, so the program will try to see if f1 can be the conclusion of QR1 or QR2. If it can be, then the program will loop into trying to prove the corresponding premise,( i.e. it will run the "auto" command on the premise).

If proving through QR1 and QR2 also fails, then it will finally try to prove using PC2 inference rule. The good thing is that sequent calculus can also give the exact atomic propositional formulas which if proven, are enough to prove the main propositional formula. So f1 will be first converted into propositonal form, then sequent calculus will be used to find smaller propositional formuale, which if proven will be enough to prove propositional form of f1. These smaller propositional formulae will be converted back to their 1st order form by using the reverse encoding  from which f1 was encoded. Then these smaller 1st order formulae will be attempted to be proven by the "auto" command in recursion.

You can create a new module for this, if you like, else you can continue in any of the existing modules. You can ask any doubt from me.
</USER_REQUEST>

<USER_REQUEST>
/grill-me Well done. Now we will be introducing 4 new REPL commands with a complicated usage pattern:-

1. "simp_l_eq t1 r1 2 t2" -> Here r1 is the name of an already proven atomic formula of type "T3 = T4" where T3 and T4 are some terms. t1 is also the name of a term in whose definition, the program will search the occurence of T3. Then the 2nd ocurence of T3 in definition of t1 will be simply replaced by T4. The new term created will be stored with the name t2(which is a previously unused name). eg:- Suppose t1 is defined as "x + y + x" and r1 is defined as "x = S z" then t2 will be defined as "x + y + S x".

There are several variants of this method:-
(i) The user may type just "simp_l_eq t1 r1 2" which would mean that the replacement should happen in place.
(ii) If the user types "simp_l_eq t1 r1 t2" then the replacement should happen at all occurences of T3 in the definition of t1.
(iii) Now you can guess what would "simp_l_eq t1 r1" would mean.
(iv) Also the user may type "simp_l_eq f2 r1 2 f3" where f2 is the name of an already created 1st order formula. The replacement will happen in the same way and the new formula will be saved with name f3(which is either a previously unused name or the name of a 1st order formula with exact same definition). Further if f2 was already proven then f3 will also become proven theorem.
(v) Additionally, the user may also write "simp_l_eq f2 r1 2 f3 f4" which will perform the above process but also create a new formula f4 defined as (definition of f2) ⇔ (definition of f3) which will also become a proven theorem. Again f4 is either a previously unused name of the name of a formula with exact same definition.
(vi) They user may also write "simp_l_eq f2 r1 2" which would mean the replacement to happen in-place. If f2 was already proven, then this change should also be reflected there.
(vii, viii and ix) In the above 3 variants, the user may omit the index meaning the replacement to occur at every index.
(x) The user may also write "simp_l_eq r1 2 f2" meaning t
<truncated 2830 bytes>
nment only because it is not allowed to change objects of parent environment. Also regarding all the goal statement changing substitutions, if the new goal is already proven then the mission will be immideately closed.

Since there are various similar looking ways of using the commands, so you may get confused. If you have any doubts, you may ask me. Also you have to very meticulously explain about the usage of these REPL commands in the "help" or "guide".
</USER_REQUEST>

Ok, now I want you to create 2 new REPL commands:-
1. "neg- f1 2 f2 f3" -> Here f1 is the name of an 1st order formula created in the current environment having double negations (¬¬) at some places. This command will remove the double negation at the 2nd index, creating a new formula named f2(which is previously an unused name or the name of an already created 1st order formula with the exact same definition). If f1 was already proven then so will be f2. Also a new formula defined as (definition of f1) ⇔ (definition of f2) will be created and saved with the name f3 which will also be a proven theorem. If f3 is not provided then it will not form. If f2 and f3 are not provided then replacement happens in place. If index is not provided then replacement happens everywhere. If f1 and f3 are not provided then replacement happens in goal statement and will be saved with the name f2. If index is 0 and f1, f3 are not provided then replacement happens in the goal statement everywhere.

2. "neg+ f1 2 f2 f3" -> Just like above but here we adding double negation.

<USER_REQUEST>
Ok I noticed that the "apply" REPL command has been implemented incorrectly. I also I want some modifications in that command also. Let me completely restate again how I want to use it:-
1. "apply E1" -> This will apply E1 axiom to prove the goal statement. If succesful, it will close the mission. In place of E1, there can be any other logical or non-logical axiom.
2. "apply PC1 f1 f2 ... fn" -> This will apply PC1 inference rule taking f1, f2 ... fn as premises and attempt to prove goal statement. Other inference rules can also be used.
3. "apply2 QR1 f1" -> This command will construct a premise which would be required to prove the goal statement using QR1 inference rule and name it as f1. If succesful, then the goal statement will simply be changed to f1.
4. "apply3 f1 f2" ->  This will use an already proven theorem named f1 of the form Ψ ⇒ Φ where Φ is the goal statement. It will just change the goal statement to Ψ and name it as f2 which is previously an unused name or the name of an already created 1st order formula with the exact same definition.

Also update the guide regarding this command

Just like ∃!x Ψ(x) is used to define a new iota function which can then unfolded when inside a formula, there is also an epsilon operator for defining epsilon functions when statements of the form ∃x Ψ(x) arearityen (only existential). Such functions can also be unfolded but in a rather simpler way. I want you to implement epsilon functions exactly like iota functions i.e. create a new epsilon REPL command having exactly same syntax as iota then store the corresponding epsilon function with correct arity as an environment object then allow a new variant of the fold command to unfold epsilon functions. Notice that expansion of iota functions would require 2 new variables(u and v in the code you wrote) after expansion. Epsilon functions would require only 1 new variable after expansion which will be provided by the user, so the REPL command syntax will have 1 argument for this variable(just like 2 for iota REPL command).

<USER_REQUEST>
Mathematicians frequently use set builder notation to denote set in formulae, which I want to implement now. So the user writes {x∈A | Ψ} to denote a term where x and A are some already created variable names and Ψ is a formula. First of all you have to update the parser and lexer to accept this as a term, so you have to create a new node for it in AST assuming it always behaves as a term. Opening and closing of a set will always be done by opening and closing braces, but note that there may or may not be any whitespaces just before or after opening and closing braces. Our program can treat set-builder terms just like epsilon terms, and their arity will be the number of free variables in Ψ including A and excluding x(handle edge cases where x and A may or may not be free in Ψ). Then you can update the fold REPL command to also unfold sets in the same way as epsilon functions. Unfolding them will also require 1 new variable which will be provided by the user just like the epsilon function. If the user types "fold { 3 f1 y f2 f3" then the 3rd occurence of a set in the formula named f1 will be unfolded using the new variable y and the new formula created will be named as f2. If f1 is already proven then so will be f2. If f3 is also provided then create a new formula named f3 defined as (definition of f1) ⇔ (definition of f3) and save it as a proven theorem also(The REPL command has exactly same structure as fold ∃!).
</USER_REQUEST>

<USER_REQUEST>
Ok I want a slight modification in the usage of this command but since there are several ways of using it, it may become confusing. So you have to listen carefully to me what I am saying. If you have any doubts you can ask question.

There are 3 arguments which take some formula as input which are <formula>, then <out>, then [f3]. You clearly understand the purpose of f3, so if only 2 formula arguments are provided then it is clear that it is the [f3] which is not provided.

However there is a desirable complication which I want to introduce when only 1 formula is provided, for example a person writes "fold ∃ f1". Then whether f1 belongs to <formula> or <out> depends on a condition. The condition is that first it will be checked if f1 is an already defined formula or not. If not then it must be the <out> argument. This implies that the current environment should not be the ground environment. Now if f1 is an already defined 1st formula then the next condition that will be check is that whether f1 was created in the current environment or some older one. If it was defined in some older environment then it can't be modified so it again has to be the <out> argument. Now suppose f1 was defined in the current environment only then it will be checked whether the current environment is ground environment or not. If it is, then there is no goal statement, so f1 will be the <formula> argument, meaning the replacement will happen in-place. If the current environment is not ground environment then the next thing will be check is whether the goal statement's name is itself f1 or not. If it is then f1 will be the <formula> argument since using it as the <out> argument will definitely fail because new definition will definitely not match old definition. This means that the goal statement's definition itself will change without changing goal statement's name. If however f1 is not the goal statement, then an attempt will be made to put f1 as the <out> argument, i.e. the expansion will happen at the goal statement's definition such that the new definition must match f1's definition exactly. Then f1 will become the new goal. However if the definition does not match then f1 will be asumed to be <formula> argument and expansion will happen in-place. If that fails then error will be shown. Also if f1 was an already created other symbol than 1st order formula then also error should be shown.

I hope I have covered all the edge cases. After you implement this, you search if a similar if else ladder can also be implemented for some other REPL command. You ask that to me then I will tell what to do.
</USER_REQUEST>

Now I want to bring "intro" REPL command also in same syntax as fold. So the new syntax will be "intro <target> <term> <out> <equiv>". You understand very well what do the arguments mean here. The 1-argument rule would not be required because <term> will always separate <target> and <out>. If <target> is mentioned and is a 1st order formula of type ∀x Ψ(x) then x will be instantiated with <term> then saved as <out> if mentioned else in-place. If <target> is not mentioned and goal statement is of type ∀x Ψ(x) then <term> must be a previously unused name to be used as a new variable(this variable object will be created in the current environment). If <target> is not mentioned and goal statement is of type ∃x Ψ(x) then x with be instantiated with <term>. If <target> is mentioned and is a 1st order formula of type ∃x Ψ(x) then again <term> must be a previously unused name to be used as a new variable. I hope this will not create any inconsistency issues. Since "intro2" is covered in this, so delete it.

Ok fine, now I am getting some idea. We can use the relation AST node to simulate atomic formula schemas. But user defined relations serve a specific purpose, so we should create a 3rd type of Relation which we can call as "r_schema". Then we can introduce a new REPL command where the user will write "crs Ψ 2" to mean create an atomic relation schema named Ψ with arity 2. Then the user will be able to use it normally just like other formulae and will also be able to prove it using axioms and theorems.

Then for instantiation, we will introduce another REPL command in with the syntax "intro2 <target> <r_schema> <f1> [<out>] [<equiv>]" which will replace an atomic relation schema in the target formula with the formula named f1. For this to be possible, f1 must have atleast as many free variables as in r_schema. Before the replacement to happen, it is necessary to establish an exact match of the free variables in r_schema to f1. The program will explicitly ask from the user which free variable of f1 will be replaced with each free variable of r_schema. Then the program also has to check that this free variable replacement does not lead to variable capture. You already know how what does <out> and <equiv> argument do. Since it does not make since to use this REPL command for goal statements so <target> argument is mandatory. The <equiv> formula should be an implication.

In a similar fashion, I would also like you to create a new type of function AST node to simulate atomic term schema called "f_schema". In an analogous fashion, it can be created by typing "cfs T 2". The intro2 command should also be able to instantiate it where target can be either a term or a 1st order formula.

If you have any doubts, ask me, else proceed

I want you to introduce a 2 new very important commands "undo" and "redo". The name itself explains its intended purpose. The challenge is that if last command created some environment object or proved some theorem, then undo should delete it, or if it deleted some theorem then it should restore it. If the last command created some mission then undo should destroy and come back to parent environment. If the last command resolved some mission or terminated it before completion then undo should restore it as well as all its environment objects back. I hope the intended purpose of undo and redo is clear in every scenario.

Repeated undos should keep undoing the last commands and repeated redos should bring them back. Undo operations can be used upto the point of last "load" or "load_h" REPL commands, or when the program started(which is from nothing). The biggest challenge is how to exactly implement all these changes. Since the program is storing the history of all the commands input by the user, so this should be able to help a lot but still some tasks like recovering deleted environment objects or storing back closed missions would become a lot difficult. First try to come up with an implementation plan how will the undo and redo behave in every scenario and how will you implement it. I think you can think this for most of the scenarios but if you feel there are a lot of difficulties in implementing it for the object restoring scenarios then we can discuss skipping that but you must mention what you think you can do.

One more advantage will be that we can allow the user to manually empty the recycle bin manually by some command or he can also check the number of contents or amount of storage occupied by recycle bin. In case the recycle bin has too much storage then it can give warnings to the user. For further optimisations, we can avoid the recycle bin to be always consuming the RAM. Some very old content can be transferred to secondary storage of the computer because it will likely not be used. This process can be automatic and/or manual(via some REPL command).

<USER_REQUEST>
I think we are making it even simpler. We don't need any timestamp, global step, undo record, undo stack or redo stack. We will just be using recycle bins, one will be permanent and other will be temporary but both of them will be implemented using stack data structure. Both of them will be initialised as empty when program starts or ends, or when load or load_h command is invoked. Now whenever the user executes dt command, or some command which renames an object(eg:- in-place modification) or some command which closes an environment then instead of deleting it, it is pushed on top of the permanent recycle bin.

Now whenever the user types undo then a pointer is initialised pointing to the last line in the history_commands list. It then reads it. If the last command created some objects then they will be now pushed to the temporary recylce bin. If the line destroyed some objects, then they must be in the permanent recycle bin so they will popped and put back in environment. If the line is "save" or "save_h" then nothing is done.

Now suppose the user types undo again then the pointer moves one line up and the same operations are performed. Now suppose the user types redo then the pointer reads the current line. If the line mentions about creation of some object then that object must have been previously put by undo to temporary recycle bin, so it will be popped back now into the environment. If the line mentions about deletion of some object then that object must have been popped back from the permanent recyclce bin by undo, so now it will be put back into the permanent recycle bin. save and save_h will again be skipped. Finally the pointer will move one line down.

In this way the user can type any sequence of undos and redos. Suppose the pointer has come all the way back to the 1st line of history_commands list, then the user again types undo then error should be shown. Suppose the pointer is at last line of history_commands list then the user types redo then the corresponding operations will be performed and pointer will simply be deleted. Typing redo again should so error. Typing undo again should bring back the pointer to the last line and corresponding operations should be executed.

Now suppose after a valid sequence of undos and redos, the user types any other command, then the temporary recycle bin will be completely emptied(hence the name temporary) and all the lines in the history_commands starting from the line at which the pointer currently is will be deleted. Then the pointer will be deleted and user's command will be executed.

I have provided very detailed execution of the whole plan, so there should not be any confusion. Just ensure that I have propely taken into account all the edge cases. Don't you think this implementation is surprisingly simpler with very low cost on memory and time? If you have any doubts regarding implementation then ask me
</USER_REQUEST>

<USER_REQUEST>
Ok I wanted to introduce a deliberate complication in the set builder parsing. The most general syntax of a set is {<variable> ∈ <term> | <formula>}. The way parser works is that as soon as it detects '{', it denotes the beginning of a set and the next '}' denotes the closing of the set. Now the parser has to identfy the location of '|', because once it does that, it is guaranteed that there is exactly one '∈' between '{' and '|' so it can easily find it. Hence it will be able to find the <variable>, <term> and <formula> argument. Now the complication lies in finding the correct '|' because it may happen this symbol may also be used by the user for some other purpose, eg:- mathematicians often use it to denote determinant, modulus and norm whereas computer scientists often use it to denote 'or' operation. So the '|' symbol may be used in the <term> or <formula> argument also making it difficult to decide which is the correct '|' symbol for set. So I want that the way parser handles this is that it picks up all the '|' symbol inside the set one by one from left to right and each time checks whether the obtained string is of the form {<variable> ∈ <term> | <formula>} or not where <term> and <fomrula> must be defined with correct syntax. As soon as it finds one, it becomes the defining symbol for set. I hope you understand. If you have any doubt, you can ask
</USER_REQUEST>

<USER_REQUEST>
Ok fine. In future we will be removing some more commands in the streamlit version, then you have to understand that the terminal version should not be affected.

Now we will be focussing upon improving the command writing experience for the user. We will be focussing deeply on this because it completely decides how user friendly our program will be. My ambition is to replace pen and paper for theorem proving in mathematics. Now currently the user just writes the command from keyboard in the console. I want that to mke this more interactive. The 1st feature which I am thinking about is to show suggestion while typing, much like the keyboard suggestions which someone sees while typing on android phone(eg:- in whatsapp). Here we dont need any ML algorithm to generate the suggestions, just show all the possible keywords which the user can enter. If we combine all the environment objects plus the special symbols(like logical connectives and quantifiers), we will be getting probably around a hundred suggestions. But all of them are not required. When the user is typing something, it must make sense. For example, if the user wrote ∀, then it must be followed by a variable so only the variables should be suggested. In a similar way, regarding everything only relevant suggestions need to shown which dont break the syntax.

So in the beginning, it should only show the REPL commands. If the user types 'a' then show only those REPL commands starting with a(eg:- apply, and). Then suppose the user types some name and presses space then the program should check if the user entered a valid name or not. If it is invalid name(i.e. there exist no REPL command with that name) then a thin red cross symbol in a thin red circle shown be shown on the right of the console and "invalid REPL command" should be written in brackets. Suggestion should not be shown if the name is invalid.

Suppose the user typed "fold" and then a whitespace. Now the suggestions should be quantifier symbols, names of user-defined functions and relations, iota function names, epsilon function names and the keyword "all". Again as the user types letters, the suggestions will reduce in number. If he/she types something invalid then again the error should be shown. You have to similarly think for each REPL command what the suggestions should be.

There will be no suggestions regarding the <occ> argument. For <target> argument, it will suggest formula names. For <out> and <equiv> argument, it will not suggest anything because they are new names.

Now there are some REPL commands where the user actually has to write definition of a term or formula. This becomes quite complicated and how you have to think how to handle this. You know what is the correct syntax for defining terms and formula which has been specified by the parser and lexer. On the basis of that you have to think what should be allowed at a specific position while defining the formula and accordingly show the suggestions(This is a tough job. You have to think hard for figuring out what all can be suggested at a specific place).
</USER_REQUEST>

I made some comments in the implementation plan. Additionally, also put following the following REPL commands:-
1. When the NAME of an unproven non-goal formula is clicked, then show mission, contra, apply, auto, search, backward_search, advanced_search commands.

Fine. Now before moving onto to improving the UI elements even more, I want to introduce some very big changes in the fundamental level. Actually I was trying to prove several theorems and I realised that the way I am using iota and epsilon operator in the program is not good because there are certain scenarios where current approach will not be beneficial(will discuss them later). Basically I want that instead of separately defining iota and epsilon functions, the user uses ε x Ψ(x) for epsilon operator and ι x Ψ(x) for iota operator. So the syntax looks similar to those of quantifiers except that applying quantifiers create a formula. In a nutshell, I want you to do following changes:-

1. Remove iota and epsilon AST node completely.
2. Remove "iota" and "epsilon" REPL commands completely.
3. Modify the parser and lexer to understand that whenever ε or ι is used in the definition of a term or formula then handle the epsilon or iota operator accordingly respectively. Syntax rules should be similar to quantifiers.
4. In the "fold" REPL command, since iota functions and epsilon functions are not present so the symbol variant will not only unfold user defined functions and relations. However we need to introduce 2 new variants of "fold" for unfolding ε and ι operators. Their syntax should be analogous to "fold ∃" and "fold ∃!" ig. Keep the unfolding logic similar to the previous one i.e. if new variable needs to be introduced then ask them from the user.

We have been dealing with equality till now which was also a binary relation. A relation applied upon terms is what we called as an *atomic formula*, which is one type of *formula*. Truth value can only be assigned to formulas and not terms, just like in english only sentences can be true or false and not phrases themselves. That is why only formula can be proven and not terms. Actually there is a simpler way to implement level 21 without even requiring the injection axiom. We just define P x as ε y (S y = x) instead of using ι operator. No I don't like the sequence. Let me just tell you the level sequence:-

Level 1 should about creating terms(ct command). Give some simple example.

Level 2 should be about mission command where the 1st hint should be "Rene Descartes said that in order to solve a complex problem, break it down into smaller sub-problems such that each sub-problem can be easily solved. Following the same analogy, if a mathematician wants to prove some complicated theorem, he wants finds what will be the important *lemmas* to prove then he restricts all his attention to proving the lemma so that he can better focus on a narrow goal because of limited memory(just like limited context window of an LLM). Mission allows to create *sub-missions* where you will have to prove a *goal statement*(lemma). Each mission has its own *environment objects*(variables, functions, relations, terms, formulae, theorems). Once the goal formula is proven then the *current active mission* closes and all its environment objects are deleted and the goal formula is proven in the *parent environment*. Or you can type exit to prematurely close the current environment, returning back to the parent environment without proving the goal formula". The last hint should  mention about creating and destroying grand-child environments.

Level 3 should mention the fold command again but this time omitting the <target> argument. I hope you have already described the effect of omitting or keeping other arguments when the fold command was originally introduced. The last hint should mention about the invariant maintained by our system for consistency purposes that an object created in some ancestor environment can't be modified or deleted in the current environment. Mention how does it affect omitting the <out> argument(in-place modifications are only allowed for objects created in the current environment). A formula created in some ancestor environment can be proven in the current environment even if it is not the goal formula, but the cons is that once the

<USER_REQUEST>
Well done. Now lets proceed to create the 3rd game folder which will be "natural number game". Even though our original purpose of the ITP was to work with ZFC, but here we will use the formal language and formal theory of natural numbers. So you will have to create a new AST node called constant and update the other program files for parser, lexer, environment etc. This is necessary because the language of natural number has the constant 0. It will also have a unary successor functions(S), binary addition function(+), binary multiplication function(*), binary exponent function(^), binary equality relation(=). Just like ZFC_rules.py, you will have to create a new file NT_rules.py which contain all the axioms of number theory which are named and defined as follows:-

S_injective -> returns true iff the input formula is of type S x = S y ⇒ x = y

0_pred -> returns true iff the input formula is of type ¬∃x S x = 0

induction -> returns true iff the input formula is of type (ψ(0) ∧ ∀x ψ(x) ⇒ ψ(S x)) ⇒ ∀x ψ(x) where ψ can be any type of formula with atleast one free variable(you will have to be cautious in writing the code for finding ψ).

add_base -> returns true iff the input formula is of type x + 0 = x

add_induction -> returns true iff the input formula is of type x + S y = S(x + y)

multiply_base -> returns true iff input formula is of type x * 0 = x

multiply_induction -> returns true iff input formula is of type x * S y = x * y + x

power_base -> returns true iff input formula is of type x ^ 0 = S 0

power_induction -> returns true iff input formula is of type x ^ S y = x ^ y * x

There is one more thing we have to worry about. Does our program allow environment objects to be named by numbers? 0 is a constant, and other natural numbers will be defined as terms in the program. I guess numbers are used in the <occ> and <arity> arguments, so my question is that will every REPL command not face any ambiguity if term names are numbers?
</USER_REQUEST>

<USER_REQUEST>
Well done. Now I want to introduce 2 new REPL commands swap_eq and swap_bi. Syntax will be swap_eq (occ) <target> <out> <equiv> where all arguments are optional. Running this command will search the occurences of = relation in <target> term or formula(which may be goal formula if not mentioned) then for the indices mentioned in (occ) argument(all if nothing mentioned), the program will simply swap the LHS and RHS of the = symbol. The new term or formula will be saved with name mentioned as <out> argument, else in-place. If the replacement happened in some term then <equiv> formula will be the old and new term joined by =, if mentioned. If the replacement happened in some formula, then <equiv> formula will be the old and new formula joined by ⇔, if mentioned. <equiv> formula will also get proven in the current environment. <out> will get proven if <target> was already proven. If <target> was not mentioned then <out> will be new name of the goal formula, if mentioned.(Everything is just like the usual behaviour of commands with similar syntaxes)

Similarly swap_bi command will search for occurences of ⇔ in the target formula then swap the LHS and RHS of ⇔.

After they are created, update the guide and ensure that this is shown in the suggestions in website version also. Also whenever the user clicks on any = or ⇔ symbol present in any formula, then the appearing popup should also show swap_eq and swap_bi commands respectively. Then create a new level in the advanced REPL commands game in the end which will make use of both swap_eq and swap_bi(different combinations of arguments). Finally test the terminal version that these commands work then test the streamlit version whether the level has been succesfully created and all the commands and popups work or not.
